> **­čôí STANDING (Roy 2026-07-19) ÔÇö CAVEMAN COMPRESSION APPLIES AGENT-TO-AGENT, not just agent-to-human.** Fleet token spend is dominated by per-turn context; inter-agent messages are a large share. Drop articles/filler/hedging/preamble/status-echo; fragments fine; no decorative tables/emoji; no log dumps (quote the shortest decisive line). Ôśů **Do NOT restate the recipient's own message back at them ÔÇö the one I kept breaking (my convergence messages re-narrated composer's/android's findings to them at length).** KEEP VERBATIM: code, `file:line`, SHAs, exact error strings, API/CLI names, config values+units, spec section numbers; never invent abbreviations (`cfg`/`impl` tokenize the same as the full word = zero saving, worse clarity). **CARVE-OUTS stay LONG: security findings/rulings, irreversible actions (flash/force-push/delete/custody), order-ambiguous multi-step sequences, REFUTATION ARGUMENTS (a compressed refutation is just an assertion), and anywhere compression creates ambiguity.** **RULE: compress the PACKAGING, never the EVIDENCE** ÔÇö the dead-observer miss came from a COMPRESSED INFERENCE ("handler exists Ôçĺ scan runs"). Unsure? Write it long; a re-ask costs more than the tokens saved. [[compress-agent-to-agent-comms]]

> **­čôĆ STANDING (Roy 2026-07-19, relayed by supervisor) ÔÇö AGENT-TO-AGENT COMMS MUST USE RFC 2119 NORMATIVE LANGUAGE.** Appended to `AGENTS.md` V2 OVERRIDE block, commit `9f883a0` on main (pure append: `git diff --numstat` = 27 added / 0 removed; 8 top-level sections before and after; `ci/public-hygiene.sh` OK). **RFC 8174 is the load-bearing half: ONLY UPPERCASE IS NORMATIVE** ÔÇö lowercase "must" is prose and binds nobody, so an instruction without a capitalised keyword is INFORMATIONAL and the recipient MUST say so rather than obeying it. This COMPOSES with the compression rule instead of fighting it: RFC 2119 REPLACES hedged prose ("it would be good if this were verified before freeze" Ôćĺ "This MUST be verified before freeze") = shorter AND unambiguous. SHOULD = MAY deviate WITH a stated reason; MUST = MAY NOT deviate, and on inability the lane MUST STOP and report rather than work around. Do NOT capitalise for emphasis (a keyword is a contract, not a shout). RELAYED requirements MUST name the source lane so obligation and provenance stay separable.
> **­čôĆ RULING (supervisor, fleet-wide 2026-07-19) ÔÇö MEMORY.md COMPRESSION IS OFF; the discriminator is LINK DENSITY.** High link-or-reference density Ôçĺ index-like Ôçĺ DO NOT COMPRESS; prose with few refs is the only safe target. **WHY it matters more than the token count: my caveman-compress defect was LOUD on RESUME.md (headings 17Ôćĺ0, ~1000 inline spans, it aborted and wrote nothing) ÔÇö on an INDEX the same defect is SILENT, the file still reads fine while the `[[links]]` stop resolving. Damage you cannot see is worse than damage that aborts.** Archival split does not rescue an index either (no dated tail to move). **Final fleet position on the three files: `MEMORY.md` never compress/split ┬Ě `RESUME.md` manual archival split ONLY (move verbatim, diff the tail byte-identical) ┬Ě `AGENTS.md` append-only, never rewrite.** hive `memory/MEMORY.md` = 19942 B, never compressed, unchanged. ÔťÄ **Correction I sent back (source lane = hive):** the ruling quotes specs' measurement (58 links / 6 headings / 4 backtick spans in 9758 B) as fleet-wide ground; that is SPECS' file ÔÇö hive's is ~2├Ś the size and I have not measured its link density. The conclusion holds for hive on the STRUCTURAL argument, but a per-lane number MUST NOT be relayed as a fleet measurement. ÔťÄ Supervisor also closed its own error: it had told the fleet RESUME.md was the per-turn token win; composer refuted it and hive+specs confirmed in their own trees ÔÇö three lanes, no repo CLAUDE.md Ôçĺ **RESUME.md is takeover-read cost only. GREP THE LOADER, never assume a file auto-loads.** The RESUME splits still stand on verified ground: both specs and composer found STALE takeover headers naming merged/abandoned branches, and composer's named a branch that STILL EXISTS Ôçĺ a takeover would have checked it out successfully and worked dead code with no error. **A stale pointer that RESOLVES is worse than one that errors.**

> **­čöĺ CUSTODY / NO-LITERALS RULE (supervisor fleet-wide ruling 2026-07-17 ÔÇö I VIOLATED this; see the incident note below).**
> Real attribution (hive_id / origin / tg_hash / hk) and any vector DERIVED from a real persona are SECRETS and MUST NOT appear as
> literals in ANY tracked artifact ÔÇö code, comments, examples, test fixtures, docs, RESUME prose, or COMMIT MESSAGES. Documenting a
> secret IS publishing it. **The public-hygiene gate does NOT protect this class** (it matches 12-hex MAC shapes; an 8-hex hive_id /
> tg_hash sails straight through ÔÇö a green gate is NOT a leak-check). Committed content stays SYNTHETIC-BY-DEFAULT; real values are
> read AT RUNTIME from gitignored custody (`~/.r2-dev-trial/*.bin`, mode 600) or env ÔÇö the hive-live-view.mjs pattern. "Lock to
> PROVISIONED" ALWAYS means at RUNTIME, never "commit the values". Regenerate vectors locally via the scratchpad vecgen harness
> (parses the custody persona with r2-trust + the real r2-wire codec); hand them to peers over fleet, never via a tracked file.

THE PIPE-MASKS-THE-EXIT-CODE TRAP, *THIRD TIME TONIGHT*, INSIDE THE CHECK OF A HARD-FAIL REQUIREMENT.**
> **ÔśůÔśů THE RULE (composer, via core) ÔÇö BANKED: *A GATE IS A PROMISE ABOUT A DOWNSTREAM DECISION. ANY GATE WHOSE ACCEPTANCE SET DIFFERS FROM THE DECISION IT PROMISES ABOUT IS LYING ÔÇö IN BOTH DIRECTIONS.*** The discriminator is **NOT** *"is the check structural?"* but ***"WHAT DOES THE CHECK'S OUTPUT CONTROL?"*** ÔÇö **diagnostic** output Ôçĺ independence is right; output that **GATES passage** Ôçĺ it **must share the consumer's acceptance set or it lies.** Ôçĺ my hand-rolled walk was **RIGHT for #72** (where `parse_persona`'s blind spot WAS the defect Ôçĺ a second instrument was mandatory) and **WRONG for #72a** (where the question became *"will the runtime accept this aggregate?"*). **THE QUESTION MOVED AND THE INSTRUMENT DID NOT.** Already resolved in `aa9d273` ÔÇö I deleted the walker before core-codex's amendment landed, for the duplicate-key divergence.

> **ÔťůÔťůÔťů #72(a) **LANDED AND FIRED BOTH WAYS THROUGH THE REAL GATE** ÔÇö rak4630-fw `50131a7` + `5a2208e` (2026-07-17). Branch-only, unpushed, nothing flashed.**
> **SHIPPED:** `crates/r2-persona-gate` = a **BUILD-ONLY helper**; private `const ANCHORS`; single public `validate_prod(persona)` (bytes only ÔÇö no table param, no clock param: neither is offered because both are what an attacker or a tired operator would want to choose); build-dep on the **VENDORED** r2-trust; calls `DeviceCertificate::verify`, never reimplements. `build.rs` calls it **unconditionally** ÔÇö there is no env var to leave unset, so **no absent-input branch to fail open through.**
> **Ôśů THE ANCHOR LITERAL VERIFIES ITSELF:** `anchor_table_is_self_consistent` asserts every entry satisfies canon's `tg_id == UUID-RAW(SHA-256(tg_pk)[0:16])`. **A hardcoded 32-byte key is NOT an unverifiable literal when the table checks itself** ÔÇö a typo breaks the relation and fails the build. **That was the last objection to consts, and the relation I derived from bytes this morning is what answers it.**
> **CONTROLS ÔÇö THROUGH THE GATE, NOT THE PREDICATE:** **positive** = `rak-persona.bin` + anchored TG Ôćĺ `credential VERIFIED ÔÇö tg_id=730c29e7ÔÇŽ role=Member (TG-attested, not self-asserted)`, thumbv7em **FINISHED** ┬Ě **negative** = **SAME ARTIFACT**, anchor swapped away Ôćĺ `REFUSING TO BAKE AN UNTRUSTED PERSONA / UnknownTrustGroup`, build **FAILED**. **Same artifact, varied anchor, both directions.** Plus **10 helper unit tests** minting a throwaway TG **in memory** (chosen AND synthetic ÔÇö the correctly-scoped use of the seed rule; **no artifact exists on disk to be mistaken for an image candidate ÔÇö the THIRD and cleanest kill of composer's gate-test-TG offer**): matching anchor ACCEPTS ┬Ě **internally-coherent-but-FOREIGN-issuer REJECTS** (composer's face-four made concrete ÔÇö *self-consistency is NOT authenticity*) ┬Ě unknown TG ┬Ě empty cert ┬Ě cross-paired key0/key5 ┬Ě window NotYetValid/ACCEPT/Expired ┬Ě signature byte-flip ┬Ě **key5Ôëáanchor (constraint 4)**.
> **CORE'S CONSTRAINT 4 ÔÇö LANDED THOUGH ALREADY CLOSED TRANSITIVELY, AND THAT IS THE POINT:** self-consistency Ôçĺ `key0==uuid(key5)`; lookup Ôçĺ `anchor.tg_id==key0`; table test Ôçĺ `anchor.tg_id==uuid(anchor.tg_pk)` Ôł┤ `key5==anchor.tg_pk`. **REFUSED TO DEPEND ON IT: the middle link is a TEST not a GATE ÔÇö delete the test and the proof evaporates SILENTLY while every build stays green ÔÇö and the last step leans on second-preimage resistance of a 128-BIT-TRUNCATED hash.** One direct comparison needs neither. *Make the bad state unrepresentable; don't reason about why it can't arise.* Its control fires **directly** (persona self-consistent for A; table maps A's tg_id to **B's key**) so self-consistency **cannot** be what catches it.
> **ÔśůÔśů TWO INSTRUMENT FAILURES I CAUGHT ON MYSELF WHILE BUILDING IT ÔÇö both are shapes I had banked hours earlier:** **(1) MY FIRST NEGATIVE CONTROL WAS INVALID** ÔÇö the staged repeater persona failed on the **OLD #72 empty-cert check and NEVER REACHED #72a**. It has **both** defects and the earlier gate **short-circuits**. I nearly banked *"the build failed"* as proof of anchor discrimination. **Verifying logic AFTER a gate cannot catch a GATE failure ÔÇö and this time the gate in front was MINE.** **(2) MY ATTRIBUTION LOG WAS A DOUBLE-COUNT** ÔÇö `issuer_anchor_fp` digested the matched **KEY**, but `tg_id` **IS** `uuid(sha256(tg_pk)[0:16])`, so that fingerprint is literally the tg_id prefix. **A line whose entire purpose was INDEPENDENT attribution was restating the persona's own claim as corroboration** ÔÇö **android's exact catch on composer's bind evidence, sitting UNREAD in my inbox while I made it.** Now digests the anchor **TABLE** (`fp=cd5eeb9f`): independent, and it changes when the table does.
> **ÔśůÔśůÔśů NEW FINDING Ôćĺ TASK #75 ÔÇö THE BOOTLOADER'S `0x22000` OTA TRUST ANCHOR IS COMPLETELY UNGATED.** core's constraint-4 premise was **MIS-AIMED at my gate** (it thought the bootloader's key5 was the persona my gate validates) ÔÇö but **its SHAPE was right and pointed somewhere it did not follow: *"ask WHICH VALUE THE CONSUMER READS."*** Asked properly, **per consumer**: **APP (baked build) reads `BAKED_PERSONA` rodata (main.rs:490) Ôçĺ #72a covers it ┬Ě BOOTLOADER reads FLASH `0x22000` (`r2_trust::persona_tg_pk`, bootloader main.rs:34; rak-geometry consts.rs:11 *"sealed TG_PK anchor ÔÇö read by BOTH app + bootloader"*) Ôçĺ NOTHING COVERS IT ┬Ě APP (non-baked) also reads `0x22000` Ôçĺ also uncovered.** **TWO DIFFERENT ARTIFACTS ÔÇö different storage, different bytes, no build-time relationship.** **`0x22000` is the UPDATE AUTHORITY** and has **zero** build-time validation. **#72 closed the funnel from a bad persona to a RADIATING app; it did NOT close the funnel from a bad persona to a TRUSTED UPDATE PATH.** **UNMEASURED, DO NOT GUESS:** how is `0x22000` written? (a) same host tooling Ôçĺ wants the same gate ┬Ě (b) only Channel-A Ôçĺ BOM-blocked with #74 ┬Ě **(c) NOBODY Ôçĺ the bootloader reads an EMPTY/STALE partition as its update authority ÔÇö the worst of the three.** Opened as a task rather than banking a story.
> **core's correction of MY over-correction, accepted:** *"you did not win a concession with a non-applicable argument in any way you should regret ÔÇö your production argument KILLED const-in-a-shared-crate, which was correct and load-bearing. It just did not reach the helper, and NOBODY had the helper yet, so no argument in play could have."* Fair. **An argument that correctly kills the option on the table is not defective because a better option later appears outside its scope.** The regret-worthy version would be *claiming* it reaches the helper ÔÇö neither of us did.

> **ÔťůÔťů #72(a) MECHANISM **RULED** ÔÇö CONST IN A **BUILD-ONLY HELPER CRATE**; core REVERSED its concession and the synthesis is NEITHER lane's original (core a64e858, 2026-07-17).**
> **THE THREE-WAY RESOLUTION:** **(i) const-in-a-SHARED-crate** ÔÇö killed by **my** production argument (correctly) ┬Ě **(ii) env build-input** ÔÇö killed by **core's** anchor-mutability argument (*"a trust anchor that can change without a commit is not an anchor"*; *"an env var is a value someone TYPES; a const is a value someone REVIEWS"*) ┬Ě **(iii) CONST IN A SEPARATE BUILD-ONLY HELPER** ÔÇö **beats both, and was neither of ours.** It exists **only because composer refused to let my "we settled it" stand.**
> **ÔśůÔśů CORE'S REVERSAL CUTS AGAINST ME AND I CONCEDE IT PLAINLY: I WON A CONCESSION WITH AN ARGUMENT THAT DOES NOT REACH THE ANSWER.** I asked core to re-examine on the production argument alone; it did and found **more than I asked** ÔÇö my objection (*"a real TG's pk must not be baked into a SHARED CRATE"*) **is an argument about a SHARED RUNTIME CRATE. A build-only helper NEVER SHIPS IN THE IMAGE, so the objection does not reach it.** **And the cleaner point neither of us made: a `tg_pk` IS PUBLIC** ÔÇö there was never a *secrecy* reason to keep an anchor out of a const. **The only real objection was shared-with-the-runtime, and the helper deletes it.** *An anchor is SUPPOSED to be baked and reviewed ÔÇö that is what an anchor IS.*
> **CORE'S CONSTRAINT 1:** the helper holds the **TABLE**; **r2-trust holds the VERIFY** ÔÇö the helper MUST call `DeviceCertificate::verify` and **never grow its own** (the gate's question is *"WILL THE RUNTIME ACCEPT THIS?"* ÔÇö only the runtime's predicate answers it; an independent impl is a **second opinion, not a stronger one**, and it drifts).
> **CORE'S CONSTRAINT 2:** the const table MUST be **PRIVATE** with a **SINGLE public production entry** ÔÇö *"if the validation fn is public AND takes the table as a parameter, build.rs can pass any table and you are back to a value someone types ÔÇö **unswappable leaks through the parameter**."* Shape: private `const ANCHORS` ┬Ě `pub fn validate_prod(persona)` taking **only** the bytes ┬Ě **cfg-test injection INSIDE the helper**.
> **ÔÜá´ŞĆ MY CONSTRAINT 3 ÔÇö NOT A PROPOSAL, A **LIVE DEFECT IN MY OWN CONTROLS**: THE HELPER MUST LINK THE **SAME r2-trust THE IMAGE LINKS** (the VENDORED one), AND THE MATCH MUST BE **CHECKED, NEVER ASSUMED**.** **MEASURED:** `platforms/rak4630/Cargo.toml:110` Ôćĺ `r2-trust = { path = "../../crates/r2-trust" }` = **VENDORED**; **my scratchpad rig linked `/home/roycdavies/Development/R2/r2-core/crates/r2-trust` = THE LIVE CORE CHECKOUT.** Ôçĺ **EVERY CONTROL I REPORTED FIRED AGAINST A DIFFERENT COPY OF THE CRATE THAN THE IMAGE RUNS.** Diffed after the fact: vendored `cert.rs` is **BYTE-IDENTICAL** to live Ôçĺ **my controls DO transfer ÔÇö BY LUCK, NOT BY CONSTRUCTION.** **In THIS repo that was a live coin-flip: #71 EXISTS PRECISELY BECAUSE A VENDORED COPY IS STALE.** The vendored **dataplane** drifted; the vendored **r2-trust** happened not to. **Ôçĺ MY CONCLUSION SURVIVES; MY METHOD DID NOT ESTABLISH IT.** And **#71 will MOVE the vendored copy ÔÇö today's match is not tomorrow's.** Core's constraint 1 *implies* this but doesn't say it, and the implication is where it bites: **a wrong path in a manifest silently converts the gate's question into *"will SOME runtime accept this?"*** See [[shared-checkout-path-dep-coupling]], [[tn-base-is-mixed-sha-assembly]].
> **OPEN INTERACTION (asked core to rule): `validate_prod` must select WHICH anchor by the persona's OWN `tg_id` (key0) ÔÇö *the input choosing its own judge*, the family we hunted all night.** **My read: SAFE** ÔÇö selecting a *legitimate* table anchor doesn't help an attacker who cannot forge a signature for a TG whose sk they lack; the lookup picks the judge, but the judge is incorruptible. **BUT Ôçĺ `validate_prod(persona)` ALONE CANNOT ENFORCE "this image is for TG X"** ÔÇö any persona whose tg_id is in the table builds fine. **That is exactly what `RAK_EXPECT_TG_ID` is for, and it lands on core's OWN split: the ANCHOR = private const (unswappable, absence = compile error); the EXPECTATION = env var in build.rs (optional but LOUD when unset). Two legs, two mechanisms, for a principled reason ÔÇö only the ANCHOR may not be typeable.**

> **ÔÜľ´ŞĆ SUPERVISOR'S SEED SPLIT ÔÇö REFUTED (chosen-vs-derived is the WRONG TEST HERE).** It proposed: TG seed = published-by-design (rule 8 recomputability), master seed = the real leak. **BOTH are the same class and it is the LEAK class.** **(1) CHOSEN Ôëá SYNTHETIC ÔÇö two axes collapsed:** CHOSEN-vs-RANDOM = how bytes are GENERATED; SYNTHETIC-vs-REAL = what they PROTECT. **Determinism doesn't make a key fake ÔÇö it makes it reproducible, which is exactly what makes publishing the seed identical to publishing the key.** **(2) The contrast class is in MY OWN RESUME:** `uuid(0x42*32)` / `hive(0xAA*32)` = chosen **AND** synthetic (no board runs them) Ôçĺ *those* are rule-8 artifacts; the repeater TG is **chosen-but-LIVE** (minted to be baked; it WAS staged `ee3b7791`). **(3) GROUND TRUTH composer does NOT treat it as published-by-design:** its own `tg.txt` header says **"SENSITIVE: tg_sk + master secrets in plaintext"**; it lives in **mode-600 custody**, not a docs dir; composer's own words ÔÇö its derivation *"needs a custody-unlocked run"*. **(4) THE KILLER ÔÇö rule 8 does NOT compel publishing this seed: recomputability requires the PUBLIC key be checkable, and VERIFYING A PUBLIC KEY NEVER REQUIRES PUBLISHING THE GENERATOR OF THE PRIVATE ONE.** tg_pk could have been handed directly (it already sits in this file classified public). **The auditability requirement is satisfied ONE BIT SHORT of the disclosure.** **(5) The split is unstable ÔÇö siblings from one file, same construction/batch/custody: applied consistently it makes both benign (false) or both leaks (true).**

> **­čŤĹ­čŤĹ RED ÔÇö THE STAGED RAK CANNOT RELAY D4's COMPACT FRAME; IDENTITY Ôťô BUT RELAY-FUNCTION ÔťŚ (2026-07-17, supervisor's will-actually-work challenge ÔÇö android's flag CONFIRMED).** My 3-way confirm-match proved the RAK **is** the right node; it NEVER proved the RAK can **decode** what D4 sends. Verified at source, both halves:
>   - **D4 originates COMPACT on LoRa** ÔÇö dfr1195 main.rs:117-119 *"R2-LORA ┬ž5.1 compact-on-LoRa (core 2026-07-10): the LoRa bearer originates COMPACT"* Ôćĺ `encode_compact`/`sign_compact`; the ef6f95a design EXCLUDES extended from the LoRa arm. On LoRa, D4 sends compact ONLY.
>   - **The RAK's VENDORED dataplane (4a3f57d) decodes EXTENDED-ONLY** ÔÇö `crates/r2-dataplane/src/lib.rs:517` `match decode_extended(frame) { Err(_) => return no }`; NO `decode_compact` anywhere (positive control: grep fired on decode_extended ├Ś5; the 7 "compact" hits are all Compact-CBOR keepalive PAYLOAD + ┬ž16.6 comments, not wire-frame decode). RAK main.rs sets NO `WireFormat` (real null: the vendored dataplane has no such type).
>   - **Ôçĺ The RAK calls `decode_extended` on D4's compact frame Ôćĺ `Err` Ôćĺ SILENT DROP.** (Even an accidental Ok would misparse the u16-vs-u32 msg_id / route Ôćĺ wrong origin Ôćĺ no correct relay. No branch relays compact correctly.)

The frame dies at step-1 decode and never reaches the exclusion I checked. I verified the relay LOGIC, not the DECODE GATE in front of it.

Core's own comment names this exact bug ÔÇö :860 "a compact-radio node that decoded extended would silently drop every [frame]"; :345 "a constrained-radio platform (LoRa/FLRC/BLE) MUST call this with WireFormat::Compact at construction, else its compact frames are decoded as extended and dropped."** Ôçĺ FIX = **RE-VENDOR, not core-write.**

>       - **Ôśů THE ELF SHA IS *NOT* A SUFFICIENT ANCHOR** (this RETRACTS the earlier "ELF sha IS the handoff anchor" agreement). composer canon (catalogue/recipes/_README.md:72-73 + nrf52840-rak4630.hive.toml:48-59) requires **THREE DISTINCT DIGESTS**: **`image_digest`** = sha256 of the RAW **.bin ON FLASH at 0x26000** (the container-independent tamper anchor a device read-back reproduces); **`flash_package_digest`** = sha256 of the **DFU .zip the tool CONSUMES**; **`hex_container_digest`** = sha256 of the Intel-HEX container. An ELF sha pins only the **INPUT** ÔÇö it CANNOT catch **objcopy offset drift** (app MUST sit at 0x26000) or **genpkg packaging drift**. **STAGE + REPORT `image_digest` (.bin) AND `flash_package_digest` (.zip), not just the ELF sha.**

> **Ôśů CORE'S "INVERTED RISK" RE-INVERTED ÔÇö THE STAGED RAK IS *NOT* DEAF (verified at source, positive-controlled, 2026-07-17).** core retracted its sx1262 clobber-fear (direction misread ÔÇö matching my independent finding) and replaced it with: *"the danger is the STAGED FIRMWARE IS RUNNING WITHOUT core's duty-cycle/RX-arming path."* **TRUE as stated, MIS-STATED as a risk.** Vendored r2-sx1262 has `SET_RX = 0x82` (continuous SetRx), `fn listen()` :525 ("enable the RX path (RXEN HIGH) before SetRx"), `fn read()` :554 Ôćĺ RxInfo; main.rs RX loop = `radio.poll()` Ôćĺ `RadioEvent::RxDone` Ôćĺ `radio.read()` Ôćĺ `handle_rx_frame(..., PHY_LORA, ...)`. **A complete, working CONTINUOUS RX path.** core's `listen_duty_cycle`/`set_rx_standby`/`set_rx_continuous` are the **SetRxDutyCycle (0x94) POWER-SAVING** path ÔÇö an enhancement; missing them costs POWER, not hearing. **Ôçĺ THE RISK INVERTS AGAIN: for a USB-powered bench, CONTINUOUS RX is the SAFER mode (it cannot miss); duty-cycled RX would ADD the [[setrxdutycycle-preamble-sizing]] hazard (rxPeriod+sleepPeriod ÔëĄ TX preamble airtime, else HARD-MISS). Recommendation: take the APIs in a snapshot if we escalate, but do NOT enable duty-cycled RX for the demo.** Corroborated by history: first light RAN; nbrs=0 was SF-attributable (DFR SF7 vs RAK SF12) Ôçĺ RX was alive, hence **benchsf7 MANDATORY**.

> **­čŤĹ­čŤĹ­čŤĹ FLASH-BLOCKER ÔÇö THE STAGED PERSONA HAS AN EMPTY CERTIFICATE. `ee3b7791` WAS NEVER FLASHABLE. (core-codex filed, core re-derived, I VERIFIED FROM THE BYTES, 2026-07-17.)**
>   - **MEASURED (my own independent hand-decode of the 188B `persona-rak-repeater.bin`):** `a7` map(7); key `0x00` text(36) tg_id; `0x01/0x02/0x03` bytes(32) dek/hk/master; **Ôśů key `0x04` Ôćĺ header `0x40` = bytes(0) = EMPTY CERT**; `0x05` bytes(32) tg_pk; `0x06` uint. **NEGATIVE CONTROL ÔÇö and it sat in the SAME DIRECTORY the whole time: `rak-persona.bin` / `d4-persona.bin` / `xiao-persona.bin` (336B each) ALL carry key04 = `04 58 93` = bytes(147) = a real cert147.** `336-188 = 148` = exactly the missing cert + header ÔÇö the arithmetic confirms the decode.
>   - **ÔśůÔśůÔśů WHY MY "EXEMPLARY" 3-WAY PROOF MISSED IT ÔÇö THE DEEPEST LESSON OF THE CAMPAIGN, and it detonated MY OWN RULE ON MY OWN FLAGSHIP PROOF.** `tg_hash`/`wire_id`/`rbid` **all derive from key0 (tg_id) + key3 (master) (+ key2 hk)**. So my confirm-match ranged over keys **0/1/2/3/5** and was **STRUCTURALLY INCAPABLE** of saying anything about **key 4**. core's formulation, exactly right: **"A PROOF THAT THE GOOD FIELDS ARE GOOD IS NOT A PROOF THAT THE BAD FIELD IS ABSENT."** **My positive control DID fire ÔÇö on the wrong fields.** Ôçĺ **SCOPE-IS-PART-OF-THE-METHOD, sharpened: a positive control must fire ON THE FIELD IN QUESTION, not merely somewhere in the artifact.** I taught the fleet that rule tonight; my flagship proof violated it, and three lanes (supervisor "exemplary", composer "the model", core "the right kind of evidence") all praised it ÔÇö **peer praise is not coverage.**
>   - **Ôśů COMPOUNDING ÔÇö THE INSTRUMENT WAS THE BLIND SPOT: my verification tool was `r2_trust::parse_persona`, and it returns `Ok` on an empty cert.** The tool I verified WITH is the tool that CANNOT SEE the defect. Ôçĺ core's fix is the right SHAPE: **require cert147 BY TYPE so an empty cert is UNREPRESENTABLE ÔÇö a CONSTRUCTION, not a check** ([[never-conclude-from-a-null]]'s "convert convention Ôćĺ construction"). **It makes my old proof impossible to write.** core's hardened parser will make the CURRENT artifact FAIL TO PARSE ÔÇö that is the point; re-mint and fix land together.
>   - **Ôśů IDENTITY, THIRD AXIS, SAME DAY: identity Ôëá FUNCTION (the compact silent-drop) ┬Ě identity Ôëá CONTROL-FLOW (the fail-open) ┬Ě identity Ôëá COMPLETENESS (this).** I proved the persona **IS** the right identity; never that it is a **COMPLETE** persona. **One artifact, three axes, and I kept re-verifying the axis I had already verified.** [[identity-verified-is-not-function-verified]].
>   - **SAME WOUND AS #72:** build.rs embeds `RAK_PERSONA_PATH` **raw, no parse** (:96-107) Ôçĺ an invalid persona is embedded silently; main.rs then maps parse-failure Ôćĺ **RADIATING KEYLESS relay** (:778-789 logs VALID + enables GroupHmac). **A persona invalid in a way `parse_persona` cannot see is the worst case of both.**
>   - **3-LANE INTERLOCK: composer RE-MINTS with cert147 ┬Ě core HARDENS `parse_persona` (cert147 by type) ┬Ě I add the runtime FAIL-STOP before radio configure + build-time expected-identity validation + a direct-from-image cert147 assert (verify the ARTIFACT, not the mint) ÔÇö task #72.** **ASKED supervisor for sequencing (I want #72 FIRST + standalone ÔÇö pure safety, needs no pin, must be true before ANY flash ÔÇö then the re-vendor transplant on top; both touch build.rs+main.rs).** **Asked core to confirm the composition: my fail-stop needs its hardened parser to have something to trip on ÔÇö and I argued for BOTH (its type-level construction AND my artifact-level assert; they fail differently).** **NOT writing firmware into a 3-lane interlock while the HOLD is live.**


> **Ôťů CARRIER-ID PROVENANCE ÔÇö RE-RUN, MEASUREMENT NOT MEMORY (2026-07-17; supervisor's ask, and it was the right one).** supervisor honestly corrected ITS OWN overstatement to Roy ("CONFIRMED REAL FROM THE MEASUREMENT" when I had plainly said I answered from my ARCHIVED RECORD) and asked me to **re-run rather than rely on a 2-week-old method ÔÇö because I made three method-scope errors TODAY, so my own old method deserves the same doubt.** Correct, and it survives:
>   - **HARNESS: `scratchpad/derivemap`** ÔÇö a cargo bin on the **REAL crate** `r2-trust` (features=[std]). NOT a re-implementation; NOT the original `persona_map.py` (session-scoped scratchpad, gone) Ôçĺ **re-running against the canonical crate is STRONGER than re-running my old script.**
>   - **DERIVATION:** `parse_persona() Ôćĺ Persona.hive_id`, computed internally per **hkdf.rs:145** `derive_hive_id(master_secret, tg_id) = fnv1a_32(uuid(HKDF(master,"r2-hive-id-v1",tg_id)[0:16]))` Ôçĺ **hive_id is DERIVED from key3(master)+key0(tg_id), never stored.**
>   - **POSITIVE CONTROL FIRED FIRST:** derive(RAK repeater) = `<REDACTED-custody>` = expected Ôçĺ harness proven able to produce a known-correct answer. **RESULT: 5 custody personas derived; the disputed carrier id IS in the derived set Ôçĺ derived from a REAL custody master_secret Ôçĺ REAL, on today's evidence.** No secrets/MACs/ids emitted ÔÇö membership + counts only.

Benign. **AND I HIT COMPOSER'S TRAP MYSELF, HOURS AFTER BANKING IT: my custody listing used `ls | head -10` ÔÇö the head had hidden the very file that produced the null.** Re-ran with `wc -l`: 6 files.
> **ÔśůÔśů ROOT CAUSE OF THE EMPTY-CERT FLASH-BLOCKER ÔÇö TWO PERSONA FORMATS, and the difference IS the cert:** **188B Ôçĺ key04 = `04 40` = bytes(0) EMPTY** ┬Ě **336B Ôçĺ key04 = `04 58 93` = bytes(147) cert147**. `~/r2-weave-tg` = **5 ├Ś 188B, ALL empty-cert** (on the weave boards since Jul 2); `~/.r2-dev-trial` rak/d4/xiao = **336B, real cert147**; **composer's new chosen-seed repeater persona (Jul 16) = 188B, EMPTY.** Ôçĺ **the replacement came out of the SAME no-cert generation path as the old weave set ÔÇö NOT a corrupt file, NOT a one-off: a GENERATION-PATH difference.** Fix belongs there; and the **ARTIFACT** must be checked (336B + key04 `04 58 93`) before staging ÔÇö **verify the artifact, not the process.**
>   - **ÔÜá THE UNCOMFORTABLE COROLLARY: the weave boards have run EMPTY-CERT personas since Jul 2 and nothing broke Ôçĺ NOTHING CURRENTLY VERIFIES THE CERT.** `parse_persona` returns Ok because an empty cert parses to **`Some(&[])`, not `None`**. **That is why core's fix must be BY TYPE (unrepresentable), not another check: the cert is currently DECORATIVE, so every check that could have caught this was structurally incapable of it ÔÇö mine included.**

> **ÔťůÔťů TASK #72 LANDED ÔÇö THE FAIL-OPEN-INTO-RADIATION FUNNEL IS CLOSED (rak4630-fw `56f6cae`, branch-only, no push, no flash, 2026-07-17).** supervisor GO'd the sequencing (**#72 FIRST + standalone, re-vendor on top** ÔÇö *"the hold was on the re-vendor and the flash; it was never a hold on safety work in your own repo"*); core ruled the composition (**BOTH layers**).
>   - **(1) build.rs VALIDATE-BEFORE-EMBED** ÔÇö hand-rolled CBOR walk, **deliberately NOT via `parse_persona`**. core's reason and it is the crux: *that parser returns `Ok` on an empty cert, so the instrument used to verify the artifact was constitutionally unable to report the defect ÔÇö a defence-in-depth layer whose only check routes through the component that already had the blind spot is not defence in depth.* Rejects: non-map / truncated / missing key0|key4 / **EMPTY cert (key4=`0x40`)** / non-bytes cert / wrong tg_id vs optional `RAK_EXPECT_TG_ID`. **Build fails.**
>   - **(2) main.rs HARD STOP** ÔÇö the invalid arm now **DIVERGES** instead of building a keyless DataPlane and falling through to `radio.configure()` ~10 lines below Ôçĺ **"never radiate" is true BY CONSTRUCTION (compiler-proven no path), not by convention.** **Async loop, NOT `panic!`** ÔÇö executor stays alive so USB-CDC log + LED stay observable with no probe and USB-DFU re-provisioning still works; a panic would take the log down and leave a dark board with no reason on the wire.
>   - **Ôśů VERIFIED WITH REAL CONTROLS ÔÇö I tested my own gate the way I have been demanding others test theirs, against REAL artifacts:** **NEGATIVE:** the ACTUAL staged empty-cert persona (188B) Ôçĺ **BUILD FAILS** (*"REFUSING TO BAKE AN INVALID PERSONA / CERTIFICATE IS EMPTY (key 4 = 0x40 = bytes(0))"*) ÔÇö the gate fires on the exact artifact that was staged and nearly flashed. **POSITIVE:** real cert147 persona (336B) Ôçĺ *"validated (336 bytes, certificate present) ÔÇö baking"*, no false-positive. **COMPILE:** clean, thumbv7em, 11.17s. *(A gate reporting OK is not evidence until its KATs prove it catches the thing ÔÇö so I proved it catches THE thing.)*
>   - **OWED, NAMED IN-FILE (explicit, not implied): (a) cert SIGNATURE + validity WINDOW at BUILD time** ÔÇö core-codex's catch: feeding the **untrusted bundle's own `issued_at`** into a verifier = **expiry self-authorized**. build.rs is the only place with a trusted clock. **ÔÜá MECHANISM ÔÇö MY ANSWER WAS OVERRULED BY CORE, AND CORE IS RIGHT. IT IS A CONST IN A SHARED CRATE, NOT AN ENV PATH.** ~~BUILD INPUT = env path~~ **REFUTED**: (i) *an env path is the `RAK_PERSONA_PATH` trap one level up* ÔÇö a value nobody reviews, a file nobody diffed, **which is HOW the empty cert got in**; (ii) **the natural implementation of an absent env var is SKIP THE CHECK = a FAIL-OPEN BY DEFAULT in the gate whose whole job is to fail closed**, failing silently and looking exactly like success; (iii) **"an env var is a value someone TYPES; a const is a value someone REVIEWS"** ÔÇö git-auditable, diff-visible, unswappable per-build, and **absence is a COMPILE ERROR, not a skipped branch**; (iv) composer's production objection is answered by a **const TABLE keyed by tg_id, fail-closed on unknown** ÔÇö and **"if a new TG needs a commit to add its anchor, THAT IS THE FEATURE: a trust anchor that can change without a commit is not an anchor."** **Ôśů THE DECIDING CONSTRAINT (core-codex) ÔÇö NEVER verify the cert against the persona's OWN key 5:** the baked app carries tg_pk+cert+hk+dek+master together in plaintext, so that proves only **SELF-CONSISTENCY** ÔÇö an image replacement swaps BOTH and still passes. **The issuer key MUST come from OUTSIDE the bundle.** Ôçĺ **THIS KILLS composer's "issuer pk = its tg_pk" OFFER, WHICH I HAD ACCEPTED ÔÇö one message after banking the rule that forbids it ("an untrusted input trusted to describe itself; never let an input supply the predicate that judges it"). Third time today I banked a rule and violated it on the next claim (direction-misread Ôćĺ wrong-board Ôćĺ this). The rule is not the hard part; APPLYING it to the thing in front of me is.** composer's *recomputability* argument survives but does not save it: **seed-derivability makes the const AUDITABLE to a REVIEWER; it does not make the bundle AUTHENTIC to the VERIFIER.** Right property, wrong risk. ÔÇö in PRODUCTION the issuer is a REAL TG whose pk must NOT be baked into a shared crate, and a dev-trial shortcut becomes the production shape by default unless refused up front; dev-trial supplies its value THROUGH the general mechanism. **composer IS the issuer, and the key is PUBLIC + RECOMPUTABLE**: the repeater-TG cert issuer is the repeater TG Ôçĺ issuer pk = its `tg_pk` = the ed25519 verifying key of `tg_sk = SHA-256('<TG-SEED ÔÇö REDACTED: this string IS the TG key; custody-only>')`. Ôçĺ composer's decisive line: **"a hardcoded const would be an UNVERIFIABLE literal; a documented-seed-derived const is a CHECKABLE one"** ÔÇö a literal I cannot recompute is a literal I cannot audit (the rbid-resolve.py property, applied to the issuer). **Ôśů NOT LANDING IT UNTIL I CAN FIRE IT BOTH WAYS** (a matching pk must ACCEPT, a wrong pk must REJECT): the repeater persona has NO cert yet (that IS the flash-blocker), and rak-persona.bin's cert is from a DIFFERENT TG Ôçĺ a negative-control candidate only. **(a) lands WITH composer's cert-bearing persona, both controls fired ÔÇö building it blind and calling it done is the identical error I just conceded.** R2-PROVISION:324 (NOT R2-RUNTIME ÔÇö core relayed the wrong number, specs caught it, I propagated it) = signature ALWAYS, expiry only where offline-checkable; **no-clock never excuses a bad signature**. **(b) runtime strict STRUCTURAL decode (no clock)** ÔÇö lands with core's hardened `parse_persona` (cert147 by type); my fail-stop turns its `Err` into the hard stop. **(c) NOT VERIFIED: on-metal runtime** (no board) ÔÇö the no-path-to-radio property is **compiler-checked, not observed**; claiming no more than that.
>   - **INTERLOCK:** composer re-produces the persona via the **cert-bearing** path (**188B = the known-bad no-cert generation path** ÔÇö same one that made the 5 old weave personas, all empty-cert; **good = ~336B, key04 = `0x58 0x93` = bytes(147)**), **held pending a specs ROLE ruling ÔÇö and composer is right to hold: a wrong-role cert PARSES and radiates; an empty one now fails loudly at build.** That asymmetry is why the role question outranks the empty cert. **#71 transplant lands ON TOP of this and gets re-touched exactly once ÔÇö which is why safety-first was the right sequence.**


> **ÔÜáÔÜá I BUILT A FAIL-OPEN INTO THE FAIL-CLOSED GATE ÔÇö core's principle caught it in code core had never seen (rak4630-fw `ce69273`, 2026-07-17).** core, ruling on the issuer key: *"the natural implementation of an absent env var is SKIP THE CHECK ÔÇö a fail-open by default, in the gate whose whole job is to fail closed; the failure would be silent and would look exactly like success."* **That is a description of my own v1**: the expected-tg_id binding was an OPTIONAL `env::var` Ôçĺ **absent var = NO CHECK**. Worse than useless ÔÇö **it READ like a TG binding existed**, so a reviewer would believe the image was bound when by default it was not. **That is THE SAME MISLABELLING I WAS REPAIRING** (main.rs called a fail-OPEN-on-identity path "FAIL-CLOSED"). **I reproduced the defect's shape INSIDE the fix for the defect.** REMOVED rather than left as false assurance; **both controls re-fired after** (empty-cert 188B Ôçĺ build FAILS; cert147 336B Ôçĺ validated). core's reasoning recorded in-file ÔÇö **the reason outlives the answer**.
> **Ôśů SPECS VINDICATED THE GATE AS CANON-MANDATED, NOT CONSERVATISM ÔÇö R2-PROVISION:326:** *"Persona present but invalid (corrupt, fails self-consistency, seal/CRC-invalid) Ôćĺ the device MUST fail closed and require a physical reset."* **An empty certificate fails self-consistency** Ôçĺ my build failure + hard stop are **the MUST we were violating**, not caution we chose. Reframes #72 from "a good idea" to "the rule we were breaking".
> **­čŤĹ #72 DOES *NOT* UNBLOCK THE FLASH (core's picture-correction, and I will not let it blur):** a conformant persona in a **BAKED** image is **still non-conformant** ÔÇö **R2-PROVISION ┬ž5.1 step 3 requires the generic image + Channel-A**, and the RAK bootloader has **ZERO Channel-A implementation**. So **#72 closes the fail-open funnel and NOTHING ELSE**; **the baked path itself is Roy's call.** "Safety fix landed" must not read as "flash unblocked" ÔÇö that is exactly the **loud-fix-hides-the-silent-hole** shape both core and composer caught me on tonight. Sequencing still stands: #72 is decision-independent.


> **Ôćö MECHANISM RESOLVED ÔÇö CORE CONCEDED TO ME, I CONCEDED ITS INVARIANT (2026-07-17; rak4630-fw `0df2c85`).** Two reversals in one exchange, each on evidence:
>   - **core CONCEDED the mechanism: BUILD-INPUT (env path), not a const.** My production argument won: *a dev-trial shortcut becomes the production shape by default unless refused up front; the production issuer is a REAL TG whose pk must not sit in a shared crate.* core, on itself: *"MY OWN DISEASE pointed back at me ÔÇö a const would have been CURRENTLY fine and STRUCTURALLY wrong. I have spent this night naming currently-true-vs-structurally-true and I proposed the currently-true option."*
>   - **Ôśů core DERIVED composer's claim instead of taking it** ÔÇö no crypto lib, so it implemented **RFC-8032 pubkey derivation in pure python**, got `tg_pk` from the documented seed, and **matched it against the staged persona's key 5**. That is the difference between accepting evidence and having it. **AND its reading of what it proves is sharper than mine was: composer's argument is about the VALUE's AUDITABILITY, not the MECHANISM** ÔÇö a seed-derived value is checkable whether it arrives by const or env Ôçĺ **it never chose build-input; my production argument did.** I had called composer's *"the better half"* ÔÇö **wrong: different axes, only one load-bearing for the question on the table.**
>   - **Ôťů CORE'S INVARIANT ADOPTED (non-negotiable, and it survives the mechanism change intact): THE ISSUER PK CHECK IS UNCONDITIONAL ÔÇö absent anchor = BUILD FAILURE, same loud refusal as the empty cert, NEVER a skipped branch.** core's objection was never the mechanism; it was that *the natural implementation of an absent env var is a skipped branch = a fail-open inside the gate whose entire job is to fail closed.* **Plus core's attribution point I had missed: LOG THE ANCHOR'S SHA ÔÇö "validated" without naming WHICH issuer it validated against is unattributable; a gate that cannot say what it checked against cannot be audited.**
>   - **ÔÜá AND CORE'S EXPECTATION-vs-ANCHOR DISTINCTION SHOWS I OVER-CORRECTED ÔÇö I had DELETED `RAK_EXPECT_TG_ID` outright.** core: *an EXPECTATION may be optional; only the ANCHOR may not.* **v1's real defect was not optionality ÔÇö it was optional AND SILENT** (unset Ôçĺ no check, while the code READ like a binding existed). **I fixed the lie by removing the capability: the cheap fix, not the right one. RESTORED with the ABSENCE MADE LOUD** ÔÇö unset now emits *"NO RAK_EXPECT_TG_ID SET ÔÇö image is NOT bound to any expected trust group; this build will accept a structurally-valid persona for ANY tg_id"*. **THREE controls fired: empty-cert Ôçĺ FAILS ┬Ě cert147 Ôçĺ validated ┬Ě no-expectation Ôçĺ ANNOUNCED.**
>   - **ÔśůÔśů THE GENERAL FORM (mine, taken from being wrong twice in one file): MY FIRST INSTINCT ON FINDING A MISLEADING CHECK WAS TO DELETE IT ÔÇö but the check was never the problem, its SILENCE was. Deleting a misleading signal removes the lie AND the capability together; making it HONEST keeps both halves.** I had been doing exactly this all night in the other direction (naming gaps rather than papering them) and did not apply it to my own code. *An optional check that announces when it is off is honest; one that stays quiet is a lie of omission.*
>   - **NEGATIVE CONTROL CONFIRMED BY CORE'S OWN DERIVATION:** staged repeater `tg_pk = da1aa7f9ÔÇŽ` vs rak-persona.bin `tg_pk = 3992f89bÔÇŽ` Ôçĺ **genuinely different TGs** Ôçĺ rak-persona.bin is a **negative**-control candidate and **I still have NO positive control**. **(a) lands with composer's cert-bearing persona, both directions fired** ÔÇö core endorsed the hold rather than pushing me to ship blind.
>   - **ROLE ENFORCEMENT (core's, not mine to duplicate): specs ruled Member `0x02` canon (R2-RUNTIME ┬ž3.2.2:246) ÔÇö the RULING closes the question but NOT the ENFORCEMENT; neither core's parse-hardening nor my gate reads the role byte.** core's framing worth keeping: **it surfaced by auditing the SHADOW of a fix rather than its target.**

> **ÔľÂ ESP L2CAP CoC FIX ÔÇö co-review turn (2026-07-16): answered core's one-per-ACL POLICY Q from metal ground truth; NO edit/push/hardware.**
> Core's ARCH-refined design (fixed command slots not stack-local args; fixed NPL pools BLE_HOST_EV_COUNT=19/SEM_COUNT=10
> Ôćĺ one persistent dispatcher event + bounded app ring + app-level FreeRTOS sem/notify pool; logical channel-generation
> handle not chan*; host-owned registry). My caller-contract UNCHANGED (8 sync-Result send_to sites). Core asked ME (metal-usage
> owner) the one-per-ACL policy Q. **ANSWERED (read-only, verified against canonical `crates/r2-esp/src/l2cap.rs` @ r2-core-consolidation):**
> - **CONFIRM one-per-ACL is R2's real model.** Firmware = PURE CoC SERVER, single PSM 0x00D2 (create_server L171), ZERO
>   connect-out (no `ble_l2cap_connect` anywhere). `send_to` (L185-188) resolves by peer_addr Ôćĺ first non-closing channel; a
>   2nd CoC to the same peer_addr is dead weight send_to never selects. R2 has NO USE for >1 CoC/peer. I back enforce-one-per-ACL fail-closed.
> - **Sharpened the ENFORCEMENT POINT (concrete gap I found):** server-only means we do NOT control how many CoC a REMOTE peer
>   opens on one ACL. `handle_accept` (L398-437) has NO per-conn_handle dedup ÔÇö accepts a 2nd CoC on the same conn_handle

> - **ÔśůÔśů FLEET PATTERN NAMED ÔÇö 'NEVER CONCLUDE FROM A NULL' (saved to memory; cost FIVE lanes one day each, same shape).** A search returns nothing -> the null is read as a CONCLUSION when **the method could never have found it**. Mine x3 ('TG not greppable' = searched the derived token; 'worktrees clean' = `git status --porcelain` sees uncommitted ONLY; 'pickaxe clean' = ran it in one repo). core's ('my branch is clean'). android's ('core-ffi is external'). composer's ('no hk in the JoinResponse' ÔÇö **one message from a demo-day alarm** off a scan that by construction cannot see inside a seal). **RULE: never conclude from a null without a POSITIVE CONTROL or DISCRIMINATOR proving the method could have seen it.** ÔÜá **AND MY FRAMING PRIMED composer's near-alarm:** I asked 'does X match? if NOT we have a real problem' ÔÇö a binary whose NULL case I had not reasoned about. **When asking a peer for a check, reason about what the null would mean FIRST.** Proposed to specs as a fleet rule alongside composer's gate inversion.
> - **Ôśů FORWARD-SECRECY GAP in the join seal ÔÇö composer raised it, I VERIFIED + SHARPENED it (spec-level, NOT custody hygiene). Routed via composer to specs; NOT my lane to rule.** Verified from r2-trust source, not agreed: **(1) NO ephemeral key exists** ÔÇö join.rs imports x25519_dalek **StaticSecret ONLY**, no EphemeralSecret (ÔÜá the "Ephemeral" hits in hkdf.rs are ┬ž3.3 G1 SYMMETRIC-material zeroization, NOT ephemeral DH ÔÇö a false friend). **(2) BOTH sides are long-term IDENTITY keys** ÔÇö derive_shared_secret_device(device_secret: SigningKey, trust_group_public: VerifyingKey) converts BOTH ed25519->x25519 then diffie_hellman Ôçĺ **TWO long-lived compromise paths** (a leaked DEVICE identity key opens that device's JoinResponse, just as a leaked tg_sk opens ALL of them). **(3) BLAST RADIUS: JoinResponseBundle carries dek(32B) AND hk(32B)** Ôçĺ retroactive tg_sk compromise = **retroactive recovery of hk+dek for EVERY device ever joined under it**, and of everything those keys protected. **RE-FRAMED: capture-now-decrypt-later on a KEY-DISTRIBUTION message = a PROTOCOL property (R2-TRUST ┬ž5.2), not a custody practice** ÔÇö no amount of careful custody makes a captured ciphertext forward-secret. **Ôśů THE TENSION (state it in the same breath): the very static-static property is EXACTLY what lets composer open the seal they minted and close the hk residual with no device. FORWARD SECRECY WOULD CLOSE THE MEASUREMENT PATH WE NOW DEPEND ON.** A real tradeoff, not a free fix ÔÇö anyone proposing FS must answer "then how does the issuer attest what it sealed?" (likely: attest at MINT time by recording the digest, not by re-opening later).

So issuer-side unseal is **not a fallback ÔÇö it is the ONLY path**, and it needs nothing from android. composer is building it: custody_backend -> sealed_tg_sk -> DH(tg_sk, app mesh_pk) -> derive_join_key -> XChaCha20 open -> SHA-256 the recovered hk -> print 12 hex ONLY. **POSITIVE-CONTROL FIRST** (run against a persona whose digest is already measured, so a null cannot be mistaken for evidence) ÔÇö the rule applied BEFORE the test rather than after the scare. > - **Ôťů CORE CO-REVIEWED `ef6f95a` = PASS + "FROM MY SIDE THE CHAIN IS READY: GO TO METAL" (core state db61e4e, branch-only, 867 tests / 0 failed; RAK thumbv7em; nrf54-lr2021 thumbv8m). I RAN CORE'S PROOF INSTEAD OF BANKING IT ÔÇö verdict CONFIRMED, proof UNSOUND.** Core replaced my call-site COUNT with an EGRESS-CLOSURE proof (strictly better method: a count of 6 can't prove there's no 7th). **But core enumerated a PROXY for the boundary, not the boundary:**
>   - **CRACK 1 ÔÇö core's premise "DATA_TX_LORA is the ONLY way onto the LoRa carrier" is FALSE.** The real carrier edge is `lora.send`, and it has **TWO** sites: main.rs:5043 (the DATA_TX_LORA drain core enumerated) **and main.rs:5055 ÔÇö `build_lora_beacon` Ôćĺ `lora.send`, bypassing DATA_TX_LORA entirely**, inside `lora_route_task` (cfg `loraroute`) Ôçĺ **it IS in the demo image.** Core enumerated a QUEUE that FEEDS the edge. **Core's conclusion survives via an argument core never made:** the missed sender emits a ┬ž8.1 discovery beacon (magic 0xB2, ver 0x01, ÔëĄ17B) built by DIRECT byte-assembly at main.rs:4684 ÔÇö it never touches `encode_extended`, so it cannot carry an extended frame.
>   - **CRACK 2 ÔÇö core's "xiao_bridge_task:5419 is compact BY CONSTRUCTION, phone-originated" is FALSE.** It is an **UNVALIDATED OPAQUE PASSTHROUGH**: `copy_from_slice(&inbuf[3..3+bl])` Ôćĺ `try_send`, **no decode, no format check**. The 2 `decode_compact` calls in that task are the OPPOSITE direction (LoRaÔćĺUSB egress; its own comment: *"the phone does the authoritative verify_compact"*). A host tagging an **extended** frame with `LORA_LOCAL_ID` gets it radiated verbatim. Compact by **HOST CONVENTION**, not construction.
>   - **SCOPE, HONESTLY ÔÇö crack 2 does NOT touch the demo, twice over:** (i) 5419 is `cfg(feature="xiaobridge")`; the demo compose is `fakesensor,benchsf7,dev,baked_persona` and `fakesensor = [otaengine, loraroute, loratcxo]` Ôçĺ xiaobridge NOT pulled Ôçĺ **task compiled OUT**; (ii) independently, 5419 is the **phoneÔćĺLoRa** direction while the demo data path is sensorÔćĺLoRaÔćĺbridgeÔćĺphone ÔÇö **the opposite way**. Real property of the *xiaobridge* image; **tracked, NOT patched before Roy's slot.**
>   - **Ôśů THE PROOF THAT ACTUALLY HOLDS (demo image, by construction):** `lora.send` = exactly 2 sites, both in `lora_route_task`. **5043** ÔćÉ DATA_TX_LORA ÔćÉ senders: `mesh_broadcast:4199` (sole caller **6143**, traced to `encode_compact`) + `xiao_bridge_task:5419` (compiled out under fakesensor). **5055** ÔćÉ `build_lora_beacon` (direct assembly, never `encode_extended`). Ôçĺ **every byte reaching the LoRa carrier in the demo image is either `encode_compact` or a ┬ž8.1 beacon. No extended, by construction ÔÇö closed over the REAL edge.** Ôçĺ **VERDICT UNCHANGED: GO TO METAL.**
>   - **ÔśůÔśů THE RULE (banked in [[never-conclude-from-a-null]]): CLOSE OVER THE ACTUAL BOUNDARY, NOT A PROXY FOR IT.** *"Enumerate everything that reaches X"* is a proof only when X is the real edge. Ask **"what is the LAST thing before the air/disk/socket?"** and enumerate THAT ÔÇö a queue/channel/wrapper is an *implementation* of the edge and there can be a second one. **Dangerous because it is proof-SHAPED, so it disarms review**; its null ("no other senders") reads as a theorem when the method could never see the bypass. **Positive control: grep the PRIMITIVE and check your enumeration already contains every hit.** You pick the proxy because it's where the DESIGN says data flows ÔÇö **but the bypass never read the design.**
>   - **HONEST SYMMETRY:** core was right that my count couldn't prove there was no 7th site ÔÇö there were in fact **EIGHT** `encode_extended` sites, not 6 (**1783** + **5949**), and **both go to `socket.send_to` (UDP/WiFi), where extended is canon-legal**. So my count was wrong **AND harmless**, exactly as core's method predicts. **Core's METHOD beat mine; my EXECUTION beat core's. Keep both halves.**

>   - **CORE'S OWN NAMING OF ITS ERROR (better than my polite version):** *"I took a CODE COMMENT as a construction proof."* :5419's comment says "TX the compact body on-air"; core read that **prose** and wrote "compact by construction". *"That is strictly worse than your call-site count: you at least enumerated real code and got a wrong-but-harmless answer; I enumerated prose."*
>   - **ÔśůÔśů THE RULE, IN ITS FINAL FORM (core's sharpening of my diagnosis ÔÇö keep this one):** *"You picked the queue because the queue is where the DESIGN says frames go ÔÇö but the beacon never read the design."* Ôçĺ **a proxy-closure only covers the paths that OBEY the architecture, so it is exactly blind to the bypass ÔÇö and a bypass is the only thing a closure proof exists to catch. THE PROXY IS CHOSEN BY READING THE DESIGN; THE VIOLATION IS DEFINED BY NOT READING IT.** So **"close over the boundary"** and **"the design cannot be the search index"** are the SAME rule. **Generalises past LoRa: any "all writes go through the repository / logger / queue / API" argument is a proxy-closure until someone enumerates the syscall.** Sits beside the day's other two ÔÇö *state the SCOPE with the result* (a null needs a positive control) and *close over the EDGE* (a closure needs the real boundary): **both are one disease ÔÇö a confident green over the wrong universe.**
>   - **Ôśů MY REFUTATION OF CORE'S MITIGATION ÔÇö the finding is SHARPER than core's own sharpening.** Core softened it: *"the host is paired (r2-usb-pair), so this is not a stranger-on-the-wire ÔÇö but trusted host is an authorisation argument, not a conformance one."* Right about the KIND of argument; **WRONG on the fact. PAIRING DOES NOT GATE THE LoRa TX PRIMITIVE** (VERIFIED main.rs:5410-5419): the demux has **three SIBLING branches** ÔÇö `looks_control(0xFF)` Ôćĺ `pairing.handle` Ôćĺ `persist_link_key`; `!synced && looks_sync` Ôćĺ consume SYNC; **`plen>1 && inbuf[2]==LORA_LOCAL_ID` Ôćĺ `copy_from_slice` Ôćĺ `DATA_TX_LORA.try_send`**. The third checks **NO** pairing state, **NO** link_key, and does **NOT** require `synced` ÔÇö **it SETS `synced=true`**. `persisted_link_key` is loaded (:5220) and handed to `Peripheral::new` (:5228), then **NEVER consulted on the TX path** (grep positive-controlled: 11 `pairing` hits Ôçĺ the null is real; link_key touches = :299/:304 load, :2726/:2742 flash record, :5399/:5406-7 inside the pairing branch ÔÇö **none gate the radiate**). Ôçĺ **an UNPAIRED host, with NO SYNC, that never ran the SM, can radiate.** The pairing SM runs **ALONGSIDE** the primitive, not **IN FRONT OF** it Ôçĺ **it provides ZERO protection here.** The only real bound is **PHYSICAL USB ACCESS** ÔÇö the same bound with or without pairing. **So: not "a paired host can radiate any bytes" ÔÇö "ANY host that can reach the port can radiate any bytes."** Both of core's axes survive; the authorisation axis no longer softens it.
>   - **ÔśůÔśů NEW COROLLARY (banked in [[never-conclude-from-a-null]]): WE AUDIT *ESCALATIONS* HARDER THAN *DE-ESCALATIONS*, SO DE-ESCALATIONS ARE WHERE UNVERIFIED CLAIMS SURVIVE.** Core's concession was rigorous on the 3 refuted claims and then added a 4th, unverified, that made the finding smaller. **Not motivated ÔÇö the same reflex as "compact by construction": a plausible fact read off the DESIGN instead of the code.** The SM *is* there, *is* wired, *looks* like it guards the port. **A softening claim needs the SAME positive control as a hardening one, and gets LESS scrutiny precisely because it lowers the stakes.** Ôçĺ **Applies to MY OWN de-escalations** ("only cosmetic", "compiled out", "not on the demo path") ÔÇö each is a claim; scope-verify it as hard as an alarm.
>   - **THE PROPERTY, STATED PLAINLY (core asked for it harder than "a xiaobridge quirk", and it's right): the xiaobridge image will RADIATE VERBATIM ANY BYTES the USB host tags with `LORA_LOCAL_ID`.** Not "may carry extended" ÔÇö **ANY bytes.** An **arbitrary-LoRa-transmit primitive exposed to the host**, whose conformance consequence is that the image can violate **R2-LORA ┬ž5.1** at the host's discretion **with no code in the DFR disagreeing.** **Tracked: hive task #69. NOT patched before Roy's slot** (flashed image in the proven anchor path Ôçĺ unpriced risk, zero demo benefit).
>   - **ÔÜá SPEC Q ROUTED TO SPECS ÔÇö I HAVE THE PATCH READY AND DELIBERATELY WILL NOT PICK THE RULING THAT SUITS IT:** is an MCU bridge **REQUIRED** to enforce bearer tier on host-originated frames (Ôçĺ DFR non-conformant TODAY, validate MANDATORY), **or** is the **R2-USB seam a TRUST BOUNDARY** where ┬ž5.1 conformance is the **HOST's** obligation (Ôçĺ fix belongs in R2-USB as a host MUST; my validate is defence-in-depth)? **Beyond my patch:** if the seam is trusted, **EVERY** bridge implementing ┬ž3.5 is an arbitrary-transmit primitive for its host **BY DESIGN** and the spec should say so; if not, ┬ž3.5 needs an explicit *"the bridge MUST reject frames violating the target bearer tier"* and every existing bridge is non-conformant until it validates. **┬ž5.1 names the tier rule but names no ENFORCEMENT POINT at a host seam ÔÇö so nobody enforced it.** (Mirror of the day's other canon item: *a physical limit is not a conformance check*.) Candidate fix post-ruling: byte0/`decode_compact` validate before `try_send`, reject non-compact, real error to the phone instead of silent garbage on the air.

Routed to the LIVE thread; NOT citing the fork as canon.) IT CORRECTED **ME**, NOT CORE ÔÇö AND THE CORRECTION COST ME MORE THAN THE POINT.**
>   - **Ôśů CANON FORECLOSES THE AXIS I ESCALATED ON. VERIFIED all 4 citations MYSELF, exact:** `R2-USB.md:32` ÔÇö *"the host and its MCU carrier are **ONE INDIVISIBLE UNIT**; the USB link is an **INTERNAL BUS** and the MCU is a **FACULTY**, not a separately-commissioned device"*; `:260` *"USB is an internal bus, not a deviceÔćödevice"*; `:329` *"USB is a local bus, **not a trust boundary**"*; `R2-LORA.md:326`. Ôçĺ **"an UNPAIRED host with no SYNC can radiate" is NOT a defect ÔÇö it is THE RATIFIED MODEL.** Physical USB access = **you ARE the hive's host**. My *"the finding is sharper than core's sharpening"* was sharper **on an axis that does not exist**.
>   - **ÔśůÔśů MY ERROR, NAMED ÔÇö the 4th real rule of the day: REFUTING A CLAIM ON ITS OWN TERMS *CONCEDES ITS FRAME*.** Core's mitigation: *"the host is pairedÔÇŽ BUT trusted host is an authorisation argument, not a conformance one, and the bearer rule is not the host's to break."* Core's **FACT** was false (pairing genuinely does not gate the TX branch ÔÇö that verification stands). Core's **FRAME** was **RIGHT** ÔÇö it is the axis separation specs then made canonical, almost word for word. **By refuting core on the trust axis I conceded the trust axis was the relevant one.** Ôçĺ **Core was wrong about the world and right about the argument; I was right about the world and wrong about the argument.** **RULE: ask "is this the right AXIS?" BEFORE "is this claim TRUE?"** ÔÇö a true refutation of a mis-framed claim still lands you in the wrong argument, **and it FEELS like rigour because you did verify something and you were right about it.**
>   - **Ôśů THIS CORRECTS MY OWN DE-ESCALATION COROLLARY FROM AN HOUR AGO ÔÇö it had only one half and my own escalation refuted it within the hour.** Final form: **WE UNDER-AUDIT DE-ESCALATIONS BECAUSE THEY LOWER THE STAKES, AND UNDER-AUDIT ESCALATIONS BECAUSE THEY LOOK LIKE RIGOUR.** The unverified claim rides in on whichever one the room is not watching.
>   - **SPECS' READ ON THE FIX (advisory): (1) ÔÇö the validate is a CONFORMANCE fix, not defence-in-depth ÔÇö but NOT because the host is untrusted. Because "┬ž5.1 binds the BEARER, and you ARE the bearer."** The `faculty` framing seals it: **a faculty is the only part of the organism touching the air, so it is the only place the bearer invariant CAN be enforced ÔÇö not because it distrusts the rest of itself.** Ôçĺ **MY PATCH MUST BE A TIER CHECK, NEVER A PAIRING/AUTH GATE**: a pairing gate fixes nothing (a paired host can still send extended) **AND** would contradict `R2-USB:32/:260/:329`. Also: specs named my question a **FALSE DICHOTOMY** ÔÇö trust and conformance are **independent axes**; option (2)'s premise ("the seam is a trust boundary") is **foreclosed**, but that does *not* make ┬ž5.1 the host's obligation. *"My TCP stack trusts my own application completely and still won't emit a malformed IP packet."*
>   - **ÔśůÔśů MY CHALLENGE 1 ÔÇö "THE DFR IS NON-CONFORMANT TODAY" OVERSTATES IT, and the distinction IS the spec gap.** ┬ž5.1's MUST NOT binds **BEHAVIOUR**. The DFR only violates it if it **EMITS** extended ÔÇö and today the host sends compact, so **it does not**. Accurate: **CONFORMANT IN BEHAVIOUR but UNENFORCING**, its conformance **CONTINGENT ON THE HOST** rather than guaranteed. Ôçĺ **THE REAL QUESTION: does a MUST NOT bind only BEHAVIOUR, or also require an ENFORCEMENT POINT at the last node that can still stop it?** Canon does not say ÔÇö **that ambiguity IS the gap**. It prices the fix: *"non-conformant today"* = shipping a violation (urgent); *"unenforced"* = a defence + a text fix (not urgent). **Specs is right about the FIX and wrong about the LABEL.**
>   - **ÔśůÔśů MY CHALLENGE 2 ÔÇö ┬ž5.1 IS INTERNALLY INCONSISTENT (sharper than either of us framed).** Sentence 1: *"The extended formatÔÇŽ **MUST NOT** be used on the LoRa bearer"* ÔÇö **ABSOLUTE**. Closing sentence: *"If 32-byte-HMAC extended-e2e is ever required on LoRa it needs a **Roy-gated NAMED PHY profile** whose MTU Ôëą the signed-extended size (e.g. `SF9/BW125` = 115 B, or a BW250 profile)"* ÔÇö **CONDITIONAL**. **It cannot be both.** It **reads as absolute and means profile-conditional**; the live thread must pick one.
>   - **ÔśůÔśůÔśů AND THE ACCIDENT HAS ALREADY STOPPED HIDING IT ÔÇö NOT IN A FUTURE PROFILE, ON ROY'S BENCH TONIGHT.** Specs located the escape at SF9/115 B as *prospective*. **It is not prospective.** ┬ž5.1's ENTIRE stated rationale is the 54 B signed-extended floor vs the **51 B SF12/BW125** MTU. But **`R2-LORA:401`: `lora_mtu` BW125 = SF7-8 Ôćĺ **222 B**, SF9 Ôćĺ 115 B, SF10-12 Ôćĺ 51 B**, and **the demo runs `benchsf7`** ÔÇö a profile **canon itself blesses** (`:386` *"a labelled WHOLE-MESH SF7/BW125 profile"*). The floor-steelman (extended Ôëą54 B always) dies on canon's **own rows**: `:377` *"These rows are COMPACT-format sizes"*, **SF7 = 51 BÔćĺ103 ms, 115 BÔćĺ195 ms, 222 BÔćĺ348 ms**; a 54 B extended frame at SF7 Ôëł **110 ms**. Ôçĺ **canon TABULATES compact frames at SF7 costing 195 ms and 348 ms as legitimate operating points ÔÇö 2├Ś and 3├Ś the airtime of the extended frame it FORBIDS.** A ToA rationale would ban 54 B extended while blessing 222 B compact at 3├Ś the cost. **No coherent rule does that.** Ôçĺ **┬ž5.1 states EXACTLY ONE ground (MTU); the paragraph never mentions airtime. > - **ÔťůÔťů CORE'S ┬ž5.1 ESCAPE-HATCH UNSOUNDNESS ÔÇö VERIFIED, AND ┬ž5.1'S *OWN CITED AUTHORITY* CONVICTS IT.** Core's argument: MTU was never the real obstacle ÔÇö compact/extended aren't self-describing, so a receiver **MIS-PARSES** the wrong tier rather than rejecting it; **raising the MTU creates NO discriminator**, so the hatch licenses exactly the failure the rule exists to prevent. **CONFIRMED FROM SOURCE, and the spec convicts itself:** ┬ž5.1:326 cites *"R2-WIRE ┬ž4.3.5 **format-detection**"* as though a discriminator existed. **`R2-WIRE.md:453`, verbatim: *"A receiving hive distinguishes compact from extended format **BY TRANSPORT CONTEXT**: messages received on BLE or LoRa adapters are parsed as compact."*** Ôçĺ **IT DETECTS NOTHING ÔÇö IT ASSUMES.** The section named *Format Detection* hard-codes format per bearer, so **a LoRa receiver parses everything as compact BY SPEC** Ôçĺ an extended frame on LoRa isn't rejected, it's **mis-parsed**. Core was right and didn't need me to be.
>   - **ÔśůÔśů MY STRENGTHENING ÔÇö THE HATCH IS NOT A PHY DECISION, IT IS A BREAKING WIRE CHANGE.** If Roy gated the SF9/115 B profile, **┬ž4.3.5:453 would STILL mandate "messages received on LoRa adapters are parsed as compact"** Ôçĺ **every conformant receiver on that profile mis-parses the very extended frames the profile exists to carry.** So the hatch needs a **THREE-way change**: an in-band **discriminator (a wire change)** + amend **┬ž4.3.5** + amend **┬ž5.1**. **It READS like "Roy approves a PHY profile" and MEANS "break the wire format."** Ôçĺ **THE HATCH UNDERSTATES ITS OWN COST BY AN ORDER OF MAGNITUDE** ÔÇö a stronger reason to kill it than inconsistency: it's **mispriced in a way that invites someone to grant it cheaply.**
>   - **Ôśů NEW ÔÇö THE DEAD MTU RATIONALE IS *DUPLICATED*, so fixing ┬ž5.1 alone leaves the corpse in R2-WIRE.** `┬ž4.3.5:463`: *"On LoRa this is moot: the LoRa bearer is compact-only (R2-LORA ┬ž5.1), and a signed extended frame cannot even fit the SF12/BW125 MTU (54-byte floor > 51, R2-LORA ┬ž5.2)."* **Same MTU argument, same SF12 scoping, same death on SF7.**
>   - **Ôśů NEW ÔÇö ┬ž4.3.5 HAS ┬ž5.1'S EXACT SHAPE: an absolute rule + an unacknowledged escape whose mechanism DOESN'T EXIST.** `:453` states detection-by-transport-context **absolutely**; `:463` then says a signed frame is *"forwarded VERBATIMÔÇŽ the receiver parses it by the **carried format context**, not by transport default"* ÔÇö an exception `:453` never admits ÔÇö **and canon concedes the mechanism is undefined on that same line: *"a format-context surface to COORDINATE WITH CORE."*** Ôçĺ **the exception invokes something that does not exist, and it is CORE's crate that would have to invent it. Two specs, one pattern.** Core has routed the re-grounding to specs: **base the MUST NOT on SINGLE-TIER-PER-BEARER** (no in-band discriminator Ôçĺ mixed tiers structurally undecodable Ôçĺ **binds on EVERY profile**), demote MTU to a **coincidental SF12-only enforcer**, and **KILL the hatch** (extended-on-LoRa would need a **discriminator = a wire change, not airtime**).

> - **­čÜĘ­čÜĘ­čÜĘ DEMO-KILLER ÔÇö ON THE MEMBER (baked_persona) COMPOSE THE RAK'S RELAY LEG IS *SILENTLY DEAD*. Core found it (my GROUP-vs-relay question surfaced it); I CONFIRMED the mechanism against the RAK's real RX path. Routed the compose decision to supervisor/Roy. NOT before Roy's slot.**
>   - **THE CHAIN (core tested @9395142, 870 tests; I verified against ground truth):** a MEMBER RAK Ôçĺ `authenticated=true` Ôçĺ F2 trusts `source_hop` Ôçĺ `build_flood_plan` SKIPS the only viable neighbour ("never flood BACK to the immediate sender", engine.rs:997) Ôçĺ `hops.is_empty()` Ôçĺ `Drop(NoViableNeighbour)` Ôçĺ `relay_on=0` Ôçĺ **NOT a HoldReason Ôçĺ SILENT DROP (no relay, no SCF custody).** Deliver and relay are INDEPENDENT (`DeliverOnly` is DEAD CODE, constructed nowhere) so the member still group-delivers **to itself** ÔÇö which does nothing for the phone. **This is core's break #4, which core scoped OUT "keyed-node-only, not the demo path" ON MY KEYLESS PREMISE. My cfg error put it BACK IN, and it IS the demo.** Break #2 (any-heard-frameÔćĺlink, which core landed to FIX the demo) is what ARMS it ÔÇö knowing MORE makes it relay LESS.
>   - **Ôťů I CONFIRMED THE MECHANISM AGAINST THE RAK ARTIFACT (not reasoned):** the RAK feeds EVERY raw RxDone buffer into `handle_rx_frame` with **NO beacon pre-demux** (rak4630 main.rs:954); `handle_rx_frame` step (1) is `decode_extended` and **decode-fail `return no` BEFORE any neighbour formation** (r2-dataplane lib.rs:516-519); **a beacon fails that decode Ôçĺ forms NO link.** Ôçĺ **only decodable DATA frames populate the RAK's neighbour table.** In the minimal READ demo the XIAO emits only ┬ž8.1 BEACONS on LoRa and the phone transmits nothing Ôçĺ **the RAK hears exactly ONE data source, D4 the sender** Ôçĺ table = {sender} Ôçĺ F2 empties the plan Ôçĺ dead relay leg. **The phone sees only the direct D4ÔćĺXIAO path (route_len=1) at 30cm ÔÇö indistinguishable from success.**
>   - **Ôśů THE FLIP IS *TOPOLOGY*, NOT COMPOSE:** if ANY hive other than D4 transmits a **decodable LoRa DATA** frame the RAK hears (2nd LoRa node #66, or D2 on-air on LoRa), F2's exclusion leaves a viable neighbour Ôçĺ relay alive. So the member compose is dead **IFF the RAK hears only D4** ÔÇö non-deterministic if a 2nd transmitter is intermittent (**two runs of the same demo can differ** ÔÇö worse than deterministic failure). **PIN THE TOPOLOGY, not just the compose.**
>   - **Ôťů MITIGATION (A) KEYLESS ÔÇö ENDORSED, with TWO bonus properties.** Drop `baked_persona` Ôçĺ the keyless bring-up arm (**verified: `baked_persona=[persona]`; arms are cfg(persona)=member vs cfg(all(not(demomember),not(persona)))=keyless; FLASH.md:41 minus baked_persona = keyless ÔÇö ONE feature-token change, ZERO code**). Keyless Ôçĺ `authenticated=false` Ôçĺ F2 trusts nobody Ôçĺ excludes nobody Ôçĺ **relays** (core's `keyless_repeater_relays_the_real_apiary_frame_shape` KAT covers it). >   - **CORE'S CLAIMS ÔÇö ALL VERIFIED EXACTLY (not banked):** `R2-LORA.md:349` **verbatim** ÔÇö *"**Beacon-vs-data demux on the shared LoRa carrier (MUST).** A receiver distinguishes an R2-BEACON ┬ž8.1.1 LoRa beacon from a data frame by **content + length**, NOT a carrier prefix: a beacon is the {15,16,17}-byte form with `magic = 0xB2` at offset 0."* ┬Ě `types.rs:124` `return Err(WireError::InvalidVersion)` with `decode_byte0` requiring `ver == 0` ┬Ě `0xB2 >> 6 = 2` Ôçĺ **a beacon CANNOT mint a `CompactFrame`** Ôçĺ **core's own `Frame = CompactFrame` would have made discovery UNSENDABLE ÔÇö they caught it themselves, the first self-catch of the day.** ┬Ě `r2-transport/src/transport.rs:248` `fn send(&self, target: u32, frame: &[u8]) -> Result<(), SendError>` ÔÇö **untyped bytes, generic, 5+ impls Ôçĺ core-owned.**
>   - **ÔśůÔśů THEIR SPEC ARGUMENT UNDERSTATES ITSELF.** Core: *"canon knows how to do in-band demux, it just NEVER GAVE compact/extended one."* **VERIFIED SHARPER ÔÇö canon GAVE them one and SPENT IT ON THE SAME VALUE TWICE:** `compact.rs:54` and `extended.rs:50` are **THE SAME CALL** ÔÇö `buf[0] = encode_byte0(h.version, h.msg_type, h.flags)`. `decode_byte0` rejects `ver != 0` Ôçĺ **3 of 4 version values (1,2,3) UNUSED.** And **the beacon demux works PRECISELY BECAUSE the beacon uses ver=2** ÔÇö it is discriminable **by the very field the two tiers left identical.** Ôçĺ **THE DISCRIMINATOR IS PRESENT, 2 BITS WIDE, 3 OF 4 VALUES FREE, AND BOTH TIERS WERE ASSIGNED ver=0.** `┬ž4.3.5:453`'s *"detection by transport context"* is a workaround for a **SOLVED** problem left unsolved in one place.
>   - **ÔśůÔśůÔśů Ôçĺ THIS REFUTES CORE'S RE-GROUNDING AS WORDED.** *"No in-band discriminator Ôçĺ mixed tiers are **STRUCTURALLY** undecodable ÔÇö binds on EVERY profile"* is **FALSE.** They are undecodable **BY CHOICE**, one spent value away from decodable. **Same over-claim shape as core's other four** (prose-as-proof Ôćĺ proxy-as-boundary Ôćĺ architecture-as-mitigation Ôćĺ proxy-as-boundary-in-a-type Ôćĺ **structural-from-current-state**) ÔÇö *"count is now five, one shape"* ÔÇö **and this one would have gone into CANON.** Ôçĺ **A rule needs a ground that is TRUE, not merely CURRENTLY TRUE**: a re-grounding on "structurally impossible" gets refuted **the day someone reads `types.rs`**, and then the MUST NOT has lost its **SECOND** ground in a week (the MTU one is already dead on benchsf7).
>   - **THE HONEST GROUND (still core's): mixed tiers are undecodable BECAUSE BOTH FORMATS WERE ASSIGNED ver=0** ÔÇö contingent, fixable, **and the fix converts a MIS-PARSE into a clean `Err`**, which is the property core actually cares about: **today** an extended frame on LoRa **passes** `decode_byte0` (ver=0 Ôťô) then garbages; **at ver=1, TODAY'S UNMODIFIED DECODER returns `InvalidVersion` ÔÇö it FAILS CLOSED.** ÔÜá **I did NOT prescribe ver=1** ÔÇö core's crate, and the cost is real: `version` is a **protocol version**, so tier-tagging it spends version space (2 bits = 4 values) and makes tier├Śversion a product; a free **flag bit** may be better (`b & 0x07`) ÔÇö **unverified, and not mine to design.** **My only claim: "structurally undecodable" is NOT AVAILABLE AS A PREMISE.**

> - **ÔśůÔśů CORE'S GENERALISATION ÔÇö the most valuable output of the day, and bigger than LoRa: "A PHYSICAL LIMIT IS NOT A CONFORMANCE CHECK ÔÇö it only HIDES the violation on the profile where the limit binds."** Review question for specs: **WHICH OF OUR MUSTs ARE ONLY "ENFORCED" BY A LIMIT SOME FUTURE PROFILE REMOVES?** Wherever a spec MUST coincides with a physical constraint, **the MUST is UNTESTED** ÔÇö and the day someone widens the constraint (a bench profile, a faster PHY, a bigger MTU) the violation ships silently. **MY COROLLARY:** the constraint is often removed by the SAFEST-LOOKING change ÔÇö `benchsf7` exists purely to make the demo fast, and it is what unmasked a 7-day-old canon violation. **A convenience knob removed an accidental safety property nobody knew they were relying on.** Routed to specs.
> - **Ôśů NEW FAILURE SHAPE NAMED (core's catch, distinct from the null rule): OPTION LAUNDERING.** Core repeated MY OWN bad option ("route io_task's extended to WiFi/UDP") back at me as if it were agreed. **"An option becomes AGREED by round-tripping between two lanes, with neither verifying it."** It needs TWO cooperating lanes and NO adversary ÔÇö which is exactly what makes it invisible. > - **Ôśů WHY IT'S LIVE ON THE BENCH BUT INVISIBLE IN THE FIELD (core's catch, and it's sharp):** a SIGNED extended frame is 22B hdr + 32B HMAC = **54B floor > the 51B SF12/BW125 control-profile MTU**, and ┬ž5.2 rejects over-MTU **with no fragmentation** => on the FIELD SF12 profile a signed extended frame is **physically un-transmittable** and the bug can never show. **The demo runs benchsf7 (SF7/BW125 = 222B MTU) ÔÇö which is EXACTLY what makes the non-conformant leg emittable. The bench profile is the unmasker.** My io_task LoRa emissions are a MIX: **4 signed** (sign_extended -> encode_extended -> mesh_broadcast) + **2 forward/relay re-encodes**. HAZARD (why it's worse than a dropped frame): a Compact-mode RAK does NOT cleanly Err on extended ÔÇö extended byte0 is structurally decodable (same ver|type|flags packing) => decode_compact MIS-PARSES it, and with core's #2 (any heard frame forms a LINK) it would form a neighbour under a **GARBAGE hive_id**, then relay-opaque re-broadcast garbage (TTL/dedup-bounded, but pollutes the table + burns airtime). There is NO reliable in-band discriminator ÔÇö which is precisely WHY canon makes the bearer single-tier.
> - **ÔśůÔśů ÔÜá I GAVE CORE AN OPTION THAT DOES NOT EXIST ÔÇö corrected.** I said "gate the leg off LoRa, **or route io_task's extended traffic to the WiFi/UDP carrier only**". **The second option is IMPOSSIBLE in the demo compose.** VERIFIED: `fakesensor = [otaengine, loraroute, loratcxo]` ÔÇö **no `ble`**; mesh_broadcast's LoRa arm is `cfg(feature="loraroute")` = COMPILED IN, its ESP-NOW/DATA_TX arm is `cfg(all(feature="ble", ...))` = **COMPILED OUT**. **=> On the demo D4, LoRa is io_task's ONLY carrier.** So gating does not REROUTE that traffic ÔÇö it SILENCES io_task's entire egress. Extended-on-LoRa is not a conformance wart on this board; it is io_task's whole data path.

> - **DISCONFIRMING EVIDENCE + CONFIG FORK (android's cheap disconfirming Q hit gold; corrects my earlier 'stale' mislabel):** dfr RESUME:162-163 records a 2026-07-10 ROY-CONFIRMED phone delivery (hive <FALLBACK-ORIGIN>, evt 0x64cedb11, 6B payload SIZE ÔÇö see the correction above; NOT a value render) full path D4->LoRa SF7->XIAO->USB->phone HMAC-verified. => core-ffi USB compact DECODE PATH is FIELD-VALIDATED at metadata/size level (android's payload-garbage attack WOUNDED, not killed). BUT that proven run was (a) DIRECT 1-hop (no RAK) and (b) the DEMO-FALLBACK config. CONFIG FORK (both real, VERIFIED by parsing d4-persona.bin with r2-trust): PROVISIONED (current baked bedd8536 image) = hive_id <D4-HIVE-ID> -> origin route[0] <D4-ORIGIN>, tg_hash <PROV-TG-HASH> target, persona hk (non-demo, != <DEMO-HK>). WHICH the multi-hop demo runs (provisioned baked-persona vs persona-erased fallback) is a ROY/supervisor config decision that determines the attribution values android+composer decode to + which vector applies. Frame STRUCTURE + decode path identical either way (proven 2026-07-10). The locked KAT I 'owed' EXISTS for FALLBACK (r2-trust); PROVISIONED would need its own vector (I can now generate via r2-trust GroupHmac over the hand-built 19B compact span ÔÇö parse_persona works standalone; r2-wire not needed). Routed config decision to supervisor, answered android.
> - **SECOND decode-consistency check (android relocated the +1-shift risk correctly): core-ffi USB decode.** android's Kotlin hands raw USB bytes to core-ffi feed() (owns SYNC/compact-reassembly/HMAC -> FfiDecodedFrame); android's ApiaryReading.decode() runs on the already-extracted 6 BE payload = shift-immune. So the 0x02-strip + compact-decode live in core-ffi. EMITTER GROUND TRUTH (main.rs:5277-5282): XIAO per-message = [len u16 LE = 1+body][local_id 0x02][compact 29B], R2-USB ┬ž3.5 v2, 0x02 = LoRa transport CAPS-declared local_id (boot CAPS). DEFINED contract, not necessarily a bug ÔÇö question = does SHIPPED core-ffi feed() honor CAPS local_id + decode body as compact. KEY: the DIRECT D4->XIAO->phone path already exercises the SAME core-ffi decode -> if a prior bench delivery RENDERED correct readings (not just arrival), core-ffi is already validated. Routed to core (feed() owner) with the emitter framing; android holds the payload KAT, frame KAT is core-ffi's. Parallel to the RAK relay compact-tier ÔÇö both core-owned decode paths must match the compact wire.

> **ÔľÂ RE-PASS ROUND 2 (2026-07-16) ÔÇö hive-codex read-only re-pass of the amended commit returned 3 findings; all triaged, NO PUSH.**
> - **F1 (HIGH, CI blocker) ÔÇö first fix was itself fail-OPEN; SUPERSEDED by round 4 (see below).** The
>   `m=$(grep ÔÇŽ | ÔÇŽ | sort)` substitutions abort the docs step under Actions' `bash -e -o pipefail` when a
>   grep matches NOTHING (clean) or all matches are allowlisted. My round-2 fix wrapped the WHOLE pipeline in
>   `|| true` ÔÇö which ALSO swallowed a scanner CRASH (rc>1: bad pattern, missing grep) and mapped it to a clean
>   result. hive-codex round-4 caught that as a NEW fail-open. Correct fix is in round 4: a `scan()` helper that
>   treats grep rc 0/1 as success but PROPAGATES rc>1 (fail-closed), with `|| true` on ONLY the allowlist filter.
> - **F3 (MED, test weakness) ÔÇö DONE.** `kat()` now accepts optional `reason` ([MAC]/[TAIL]/[TAIL-0x]/[TAIL-COMPACT]) and exact `count`; high-value KATs assert them so a wrong-CLASSIFIER regression (MAC misread as TAIL, or the 4-group run's 2-window count) can no longer stay green on a bare flag/no-flag check. Selftest **41/41** with the stricter asserts.
> - **F2 (MED, false-positives) ÔÇö VERIFIED, one sub-claim REFUTED, narrowing DEFERRED as a Roy-canon tradeoff.**
>   (Examples described abstractly here on purpose ÔÇö writing the literal token beside a context word would trip
>   this very gate on RESUME.md; see the self-inflicted-trap note in memory.) Confirmed latent FPs, all currently
>   ABSENT from the tree: a time-of-day triple or a short two-digit-group date sitting beside a board/device word
>   classifies as a TAIL; a six-digit baud constant beside a board-id label classifies as a compact tail; a
>   revision-like six-hex filename segment can too. REFUTED: ISO-date *filenames* with a four-digit year do NOT
>   flag ÔÇö the hex negative-lookbehind already blocks them (the year's last digit is hex before the date run).
>   Decision: the gate is fail-SAFE by design (errs toward flagging, exact-allowlist escape hatch); every F2 fix
>   narrows CONTEXT = the fail-OPEN direction that burned this workstream twice, and the real tree is currently
>   clean (exit 0). Not narrowing unilaterally; routed to hive-codex/supervisor as a noise-vs-fail-open tradeoff on
>   Roy-canon context rules. **Do-not-assume:** narrowing the tail-context set to quiet F2 without KATs proving no
>   new fail-open is the exact regression class this branch exists to kill.

> **ÔľÂ RE-PASS ROUND 4 (2026-07-16) ÔÇö hive-codex refuted my OWN round-2/3 fixes; both were real. FIXED. NO PUSH.**
> - **docs F1 fail-OPEN (HIGH) ÔÇö properly FIXED.** The round-2 blanket `|| true` mapped a scanner CRASH (grep
>   rc>1: missing binary, invalid pattern, unreadable tree) to the same empty/clean result as a legit no-match ÔÇö
>   fail-open. Replaced with a `scan()` helper: grep rc 0/1 = success (emit matches, empty on no-match), rc>1
>   PROPAGATES so `set -e` aborts = fail-CLOSED; `|| true` now wraps ONLY the allowlist filter (its rc1 = all
>   placeholders, never a tool failure). Verified end-to-end incl. the decisive case: a broken grep (rc2) now
>   makes the step EXIT 2 (fail-closed), not exit-0-clean. CleanÔćĺ0, planted MACÔćĺ1, allowlisted-onlyÔćĺ0 all hold.
> - **kat() crash-suppression (MED) ÔÇö FIXED.** `kat()` used `hygiene_scan || true`, so a scanner crash on a
>   VALID must-pass fixture false-passed. Now captures the scanner status (`&& src=0 || src=$?`) and FAILs the
>   KAT on any non-zero on valid input; the malformed-stream crash path is checked separately. Proved with an
>   injected `hygiene_scan(){ return 3; }` ÔÇö kat() reports FAIL (old code printed ok). Selftest **43/43**.
> - **merge-legitimate-fragments precision (noise, NOT fail-open) ÔÇö documented tradeoff.** A timestamp+segment
>   like a time triple joined by a separator to another triple normalises to six pairs and flags [MAC]; spaced
>   fragments pass. Inherently ambiguous; under the fail-SAFE policy this is a noise tradeoff, not a hole. Policy:
>   keep flagging (fail-safe); if a real doc trips it, use a `T`/space separator or an exact allowlist entry.
